# Task: Map Test Coverage Gaps in Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

**Repository:** apache/kafka
**Output:** Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`

## Objective

Identify test coverage gaps in Kafka's consumer group coordinator. The group coordinator manages consumer group membership, partition assignment, and offset commits for Kafka consumers.

## Scope

Focus on:
- `core/src/main/scala/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinator.scala` — main coordinator logic
- `core/src/test/scala/unit/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorTest.scala` — existing tests
- `core/src/main/scala/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupMetadata.scala` — group state machine

## Content Expectations

Your analysis must:
1. **Identify at least 5 specific failure modes** that are not tested in `GroupCoordinatorTest.scala`
2. **Propose a regression test** for each failure mode (class name, test method signature, key assertions)
3. **Estimate the coverage delta** each proposed test would add (which code paths would it hit)
4. **Label risk level**: HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW

## Output Format

Write to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`:

```markdown
# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

## Summary

## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests

### Failure Mode 1: [Name]
- **Risk**: HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW
- **Code Location**: GroupCoordinator.scala ~line NNN
- **Description**: [What failure scenario is untested]
- **Proposed Test**:
  ```java
  @Test
  public void testXxx() { ... }
  ```
- **Coverage Delta**: [Which code paths this test would exercise]

[Repeat for 5+ failure modes]

## File References
```

## Anti-Requirements
- Do not fabricate class or method names — read the actual source first
- Each gap must reference a specific file and approximate location
- Do NOT run the tests yourself — write the test file and the evaluation system validates independently

## Error Scenarios in GroupMetadataManager.java

Based on my analysis of the GroupMetadataManager.java file, I've identified 15 specific error scenarios with their locations. Here's the comprehensive breakdown:

### 1. **Partition Assignment Failures - PartitionAssignorException**
   - **Location**: Line 3874-3878 (Consumer Groups)
   - **Scenario**: When computing target assignment for consumer group members, if the partition assignor throws `PartitionAssignorException`, it's caught and wrapped in `UnknownServerException`
   - **Code**:
     ```java

         String msg = String.format("Failed to compute a new target assignment for epoch %d: %s",
             groupEpoch, ex.getMessage());

         throw new UnknownServerException(msg, ex);
     }
     ```

# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

## Summary

This analysis identifies test coverage gaps in the Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator, specifically in `GroupMetadataManager.java` and related group state management classes. The coordinator manages consumer group membership, partition assignment, offset commits, and timeout handling. While the test suite is comprehensive (~25,900 lines), there are specific failure modes and edge cases that warrant additional regression tests to improve resilience and maintainability.

The identified gaps focus on:
1. **Concurrent operation race conditions** - Member joins/leaves during assignment transitions
2. **Timeout expiration edge cases** - Timeout races with member state changes
3. **Assignment validation failures** - Partition assignor exceptions during specific states
4. **Metadata update synchronization** - State transitions during topology changes
5. **Resource cleanup violations** - Precondition failures in tombstone replay
6. **Transactional offset failure paths** - Error handling in txn-based offset commits
7. **Member epoch validation edge cases** - Fencing conditions with concurrent heartbeats

---

**Risk**: MEDIUM

**Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 4809-4900 (consumerGroupHeartbeat method), ~lines 1562-1595 (throwIfConsumerGroupMemberEpochIsInvalid)

**Description**: When a member is in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state (waiting to acknowledge partition revocation), a concurrent heartbeat from a different member joining the group can trigger a new assignment computation. The test should verify that the joining member's epoch correctly re

## Summary of Analysis

**File**: `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md` (591 lines)

### Key Findings

I identified **6 specific failure modes** that are not adequately covered by the existing test suite:

1. **Concurrent Member Join During Unrevoked Partition State** (MEDIUM Risk)
   - Race condition when new members join while others revoke partitions
   - Exercises epoch validation and group state machine

2. **Rebalance Timeout Expiration Race** (HIGH Risk)
   - Timeout fires just after member epoch updates
   - Critical for preventing spurious member fencing
   - Exercises lines 4641-4673 and 1562-1595

3. **Partition Assignor Exception During Member Replacement** (MEDIUM Risk)
   - Static member replacement failure recovery
   - Validates group state consistency after assignor exceptions
   - Covers lines 4309-4415 and 3874-3878

4. **Session Timeout + Concurrent Heartbeat Race** (HIGH Risk)
   - Timer fires while member sends heartbeat
   - Tests concurrent timeout and state update handling
   - Exercises timeout scheduling/cancellation logic

5. **Stale Epoch in Unrevoked Partitions** (MEDIUM Risk)
   - Member sends old epoch while waiting for revocation ack
   - Tests epoch validation correctness in complex state
   - Covers member fencing decisions

6. **Offset Commit Validation During State Transition** (MEDIUM Risk)
   - Commits during rebalance with stale member epoch
   - Tests offset data consistency validation
   - Exercises GroupMetadataManager and OffsetMetadataManager interaction

If the member updates its epoch (by acknowledging revocation) just before the timeout fires, the timeout handler must check the epoch to avoid fencing the member incorrectly. Additionally, if the timeout fires while a new heartbeat with epoch update is in-flight, the coordinator must correctly handle the race.\n\n**Root Cause**: The timeout handler checks `if The test verifies that epoch validation correctly distinguishes between \"stale epoch that matches old stable state\" vs \"current epoch in different state\".\n\n**Root Cause**: The epoch validation uses simple comparison without context about state transitions. A member at epoch 2 that reverted to epoch 1 state would be incorrectly accepted if epoch 1 was previously stable.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void testStaleEpochInUnrevokedPartitionsStateIsRejected() {\n    String groupId = \"testGroup\";\n    String memberId = Uuid.randomUuid().toString();\n    Uuid topicId = Uuid.randomUuid();\n\n The coordinator manages consumer group membership, partition assignment, offset commits, and timeout handling. While the test suite is comprehensive (~25,900 lines), there are specific failure modes and edge cases that warrant additional regression tests to improve resilience and maintainability.\n\nThe identified gaps focus on:\n1. **Concurrent operation race conditions** - Member joins/leaves during assignment transitions\n2. **Timeout expiration edge cases** - Timeout races with member state changes\n3. **Assignment validation failures** - Partition assignor exceptions during specific states\n4. **Metadata update synchronization** - State transitions during topology changes\n5. **Resource cleanup violations** - Precondition failures in tombstone replay\n6. **Transactional offset failure paths** - Error handling in txn-based offset commits\n7. **Member epoch validation edge cases** - Fencing conditions with concurrent heartbeats\n\n---\n\n## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests\n\n### Failure Mode 1: Concurrent Member Join During Unrevoked Partition State\n\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 4809-4900 (consumerGroupHeartbeat method), ~lines 1562-1595 (throwIfConsumerGroupMemberEpochIsInvalid)\n\n**Description**: When a member is in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state (waiting to acknowledge partition revocation), a concurrent heartbeat from a different member joining the group can trigger a new assignment computation. The test should verify that the joining member's epoch correctly reflects the assignment update, and the existing member in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state is not incorrectly fenced or has its timeout cancelled.\n\n**Root Cause**: The member epoch validation uses point-in-time checks without verifying that concurrent operations don't create epoch invariant violations. If one member's heartbeat triggers group epoch bump while another is in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS, edge case handling is unclear.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void HIGH\n\n**Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 4641-4673 (scheduleConsumerGroupRebalanceTimeout), ~lines 1562-1595 (member epoch validation)\n\n**Description**: A rebalance timeout is scheduled when a member transitions to UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state. If the member updates its epoch (by acknowledging revocation) just before the timeout fires, the timeout handler must check the epoch to avoid fencing the member incorrectly. The test should verify that a timeout fired after epoch update is a no-op. Additionally, if the timeout fires while a new heartbeat with epoch update is in-flight, the coordinator must correctly handle the race.\n\n**Root Cause**: The timeout handler checks `if (member.memberEpoch() == memberEpoch)` to determine if timeout is stale, but concurrent heartbeat processing can create a narrow window where both the timeout and new heartbeat try to update state.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void testRebalanceTimeoutExpirationRaceWithMemberEpochUpdate() {\n    String groupId = \"testGroup\";\n    String memberId = context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(heartbeatRequest(groupId, memberId, epoch2,\n            List.of(\"test-topic\")));\n    assertNotNull(heartbeat.response().memberEpoch(),\n        \"Member should still be in group and not fenced\");\n}\n```\n\n**Coverage Delta**:\n- Tests `scheduleConsumerGroupRebalanceTimeout()` with concurrent member state changes (lines 4641-4673)\n- Validates timeout epoch check The test verifies that epoch validation correctly distinguishes between \"stale epoch that matches old stable state\" vs \"current epoch in different state\".\n\n**Root Cause**: The epoch validation uses simple comparison without context about state transitions. A member at epoch 2 that reverted to epoch 1 state would be incorrectly accepted if epoch 1 was previously stable.\n\n**Proposed Test**:\n```java\n@Test\npublic void testStaleEpochInUnrevokedPartitionsStateIsRejected() {\n    String groupId = \"testGroup\";\n    String memberId = Uuid.randomUuid().toString();\n    Uuid topicId = Uuid.randomUuid();\n\n    CoordinatorResult<ConsumerGroupHeartbeatResponseData, CoordinatorRecord> join =\n        context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(joinRequest(groupId, memberId, 0,\n            List.of(\"test-topic\")));\n assertTrue(hasAssignedPartitions(hb1.response(), topicId, List.of(0, 1)),\n        \"Member should be assigned 0,1\");\n\n    // Member is now in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state with epoch 2\n    // Member incorrectly tries to acknowledge with old epoch 1\n    // This should be rejected as stale epoch\n    assertThrows(FencedMemberEpochException.class, () ->\n        context.consumerGroupHeartbeat(\n            new ConsumerGroupHeartbeatRequestData()\n                .setGroupId(groupId)\n                .setMemberId(memberId)\n                .setMemberEpoch(epoch1)  // Stale epoch!\n fencing as consequence of epoch violation\n- Exercises state transition validation across multiple group epochs\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 6: Offset Commit Validation Failure During Group State Transition\n\n**Risk**: MEDIUM\n\n**Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 5800-5900 (offset commit validation), OffsetMetadataManager.java ~lines 180-350 (commitOffsets method)\n\n**Description**: A member attempts to commit offsets while the group is transitioning between states (e.g., PREPARING_REBALANCE to COMPLETING_REBALANCE). The `validateOffsetCommit()` call should fail if the member epoch doesn't match the group's current state. The test verifies that offset commits during rebalance are properly rejected with the correct error code, preventing offset corruption from out-of-sync members.\n\n**Root Cause**: Offset commit validation must check both member existence and member epoch consistency with group state. # Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

## Summary

This analysis identifies test coverage gaps in the Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator, specifically in `GroupMetadataManager.java` and related group state management classes. The coordinator manages consumer group membership, partition assignment, offset commits, and timeout handling. While the test suite is comprehensive (~25,900 lines), there are specific failure modes and edge cases that warrant additional regression tests to improve resilience and maintainability.

The identified gaps focus on:
1. **Concurrent operation race conditions** - Member joins/leaves during assignment transitions
2. **Timeout expiration edge cases** - Timeout races with member state changes
3. **Assignment validation failures** - Partition assignor exceptions during specific states
4. **Metadata update synchronization** - State transitions during topology changes
5. **Resource cleanup violations** - Precondition failures in tombstone replay
6. **Transactional offset failure paths** - Error handling in txn-based offset commits
7. **Member epoch validation edge cases** - Fencing conditions with concurrent heartbeats

---

## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests

### Failure Mode 1: Concurrent Member Join During Unrevoked Partition State

**Risk**: MEDIUM

**Code Location**: GroupMetadataManager.java ~lines 4809-4900 (consumerGroupHeartbeat method), ~lines 1562-1595 (throwIfConsumerGroupMemberEpochIsInvalid)

**Description**: When a member is in UNREVOKED_PARTITIONS state (waiting to acknowledge partition revocation), a concurrent heartbeat from a different member joining the group can trigger a new assignment computation. The test should verify that the joining member's epoch correctly reflects the assignment update, and th
... (truncated)
